To Thought — Mu Yin 237

To knowingly proceed towards a broken cliff and sheer wall, venturing to seek fortune in a single gamble, that perhaps is what is called being brave. To knowingly confront tigers, wolves and pitfalls, being able to resolutely turn back, picking up and letting go, that perhaps is what is called being smart. Only those who hesitate on life's path, wandering at the crossroads, feeling unable to advance or retreat, those are the pitiful and ordinary people!

I am perplexed, I am distressed, only because I have too many ordinary thoughts.

Thought! For you I have endured unbearable melancholy, for you I have felt inexplicable sorrow, for you I have swallowed all the bitterness and spiciness of this world, yearning, pondering, dreaming... Alas! Unbearable to mention!

Scattered waves in the sea of mind, forming the universe's wine glass, full of many ordinary and pitiful people sinking and grieving within; yet, isn't the cause of all the commotion all for you?

There was a time when I wanted to dedicate myself to an armed force, listening to the frenzied shouts of thousands of troops and horses, watching the tragic spectacle of wind-borne blood on the battlefield. Miao Peilin's "Man Jiang Hong" says it well:

"Alone on horseback against the west wind, how many times have I traversed mountain passes and moonlit nights! See tonight the frost flowers large as palms, the battle garments like iron, with unrestrained feelings I praise Tao Yuanming's chrysanthemums, with heroic ambition I await swallowing Su Wu's snow! Alas, the north and south of the river have all fallen, the Red Goat Calamity.

Do not cherish, farewell to wife and children! The heart is not heated by meritorious fame! Only with me is the art of war, a few leaves of Sun Wu, a fierce tiger walks into the mountains to be captured, an ominous star in the sky has not yet been extinguished; take advantage of the autumn waves to roll up your sleeves and wash your robes, in the sandy field with blood!"

Reading this, I cannot help but feel heroic and want to start dancing, but thinking: once shrouded in horse hide after death, killing all over the fields; yellow sand and blue blood, vast and boundless; tragic songs and generosity, how could it not be a hero of the moment, and how could it not be a martyr of the future!

There was a time when I thought of the illusion of life, morning dew and passing clouds, the vastness of heaven and earth, without end. I could not help but have all thoughts turn to ash, and tears streamed down my face in sorrow, immediately hoping to quietly retreat, indifferently hide, in a bay of reeds, a few rows of declining willows, leisurely in a mountain-empty and water-quiet village, listening to the sad sobs of the gibbons, watching the seagulls coming and going, with solemn and distant intent, without years, without management and disturbance, also a god in the world, so why fear others scolding "passive"!

There was also a time when I thought of using poisonous wine to numb myself, forgetting the universe, the people of the world; forgetting the darkness; forgetting the ugliness; forgetting the suffering. Everything, only crazy laughter, no crying! Its name is "decadence!" Also a secret to being "modern"!

There was an even more time when I wanted to cater to society, oppress life, wear a skull mask, pretend to have a charming fake smile, to play with everything; regardless of what I encounter is a sincere heart, or the cold water of the head! Only jokes, only cunning, and some enthusiasm! Not even fearing the slanderous words and actions of being scolded as a "literary beggar."

However, I am a young man, a young man with fresh red flesh and blood, who is unwilling to linger and steal life, and even less willing to meander to death; it has made me decadent, it will make me willing to be mad, but, Thought! What have you actually given me? A task to be done.

Hometown, by Xiao Zhi 238

My hometown. I've set foot in my hometown after a full five years of separation. Here, everything is only slightly different from five years ago: the narrow, alley-like street, perpetually covered with a thick layer of muddy, broken flagstones, is still as gloomy as ever. The unique scent, a kind of intoxicating fragrance, that faintly wafts through the air, seems even stronger! The shop signs still hang low, blocking the sunlight, their colors faded. On the street corners, the idle and carefree friends are probably not all those uncles with inch-long beards they were five years ago, constantly stroking them (truly, if I were more neurotic, I'd suspect those bearded "uncles" had swallowed an elixir of eternal youth and suddenly become handsome!). They seem to be sons and young masters from some family, mostly young lads, some carrying birdcages, with cigars in their mouths, humming "Dragon's Cave". Others wear black silk trousers with wide legs that drag behind their heels and white Xiaofang long gowns with high, starched collars. Still others are dressed in neatly tailored Western suits, their hair parted and slicked back ×× from the ×× girls' school. In the narrowest street, the one with the most shops, the most broken flagstones, their footprints are the most frequent, and they are always in groups. They are gesturing enthusiastically, winking and raising their eyebrows as they chirpily flirt and comment on the female students in black short skirts and white Peter Pan-collared shirts walking along the same road. They even speak to each other in fluent Chinglish learned from Shanghai, though the black eyes under the girls' short hair never turn to look at them, and their drawn faces don't show a trace of a smile, only hidden anger and embarrassment. Nor do they consider that the mud beneath their feet might splash on the hems of their white Xiaofang long gowns with high, starched collars, which they wear every day, or the cuffs of their tailored Western suits. They are just chasing, chasing more frantically and earnestly than they eat. Besides these countless carefree young lads who seem to be sons and young masters from some family, those who can dash recklessly through the streets are, of course, our true old men wearing white or gray uniforms with leather belts.

Page 19

Many shops are filled with musicians, blowing foreign drums, foreign horns, and foreign flutes without stopping all day, their cheeks puffed out. The shops are indeed crowded with people coming and going. Although the shop assistants and apprentices are busily moving goods around, shouting, and making a great commotion, some of the gentlemen at the cash registers have taken off their copper-rimmed glasses and placed them in the wooden tray holding their writing brushes and inkstones, lowering their slightly swaying heads and leisurely writing letters home on eight-lined paper. Others are squinting, dozing off. As for the music of foreign coins clinking together and the rhythm of abacus beads clicking, that is truly too rare and precious to be easily heard.

Wanting to taste the local flavors of my hometown, I ventured on my own to ×× Chun, a restaurant reputed to be the biggest and most famous in the city, for dinner. As soon as I entered the dining hall, I saw that every table was full. The waiter, with an oily black towel draped over his shoulder, hurried to greet me, "Upstairs, private room." So, without thinking, I went upstairs to the private room. Oh, my heavens! Red faces, bulging veins, bare shoulders, open clothes, fists waving, mouths drinking, chewing, and laughing, the waiter running tirelessly between tables, responding to calls. Wine, meat, bones, sweat, saliva, and sounds had already filled the hall in a blurred mess! Where was there room for me to sit down? I went to another restaurant, the same! Another one, still the same! Second-class, third-class, the most basic, all equally full of customers of their respective classes, chewing loudly! I, a traveler who had just returned from afar as a guest, would probably not attract anyone's attention or be given a seat. So, I decided to go to the "× Ji Old × House," famous far and wide, to buy dry provisions. But, heaven! With so many heads, how could a stranger like me squeeze in? I steeled myself, "Let's go to △ Xiang Cun!" Indeed, it was less crowded here, but only after a succession of "old customers" had rushed to buy "four ounces of melon seeds," "half a pound of sesame brittle," "two rice cakes," and "one hundred cash of spiced beans" did a round-faced, smiling clerk, covered in sweat, hand me two loaves of bread, saying they were "from Sullivan in Shanghai, fragrant and sweet." This time, the wait wasn't an hour, but forty-five minutes, a record that probably wouldn't be broken.

...Anyone who is willing to take a stroll on the streets of my hometown can see these things. Yes, my hometown, the hometown of dark, muddy, narrow streets, has become a world of young lads who seem to be sons and young masters from some family, carrying birdcages, wearing high-collared long gowns, tailored Western suits, and teasing and commenting on female students, and of old men with leather belts wearing gray or white uniforms who dash recklessly through the streets. The rest are: red-faced, vein-bulging, bare-shouldered diners, waiters with oily black towels draped over their shoulders running around and responding to calls, and old customers and clerks covered in sweat rushing to buy sweets and snacks. Next, there are: musicians with puffed-out cheeks playing all day long, shop assistants and apprentices busily moving goods around, and accountants who have taken off their copper-rimmed glasses and are leisurely writing letters home, as well as silent abacuses and foreign coins that have disappeared.

Predicament, by Yun 239

To raise the rent, which could no longer be delayed, I began to feel very anxious: if I didn't pay both this month's rent and last month's rent, which had been carried over, clearly and cleanly, then the second landlord would surely force me to move out, wouldn't he? Look, wasn't the Wang family, who lived in the large厢房 and had accumulated two months' worth, forced to move out by the landlady, all seven members of the family? I heard that the Wang family was an old tenant, and I've only lived here for two years. Moreover, they usually treated the whole landlord's family with amity and harmony, with absolutely no disputes or quarrels, and yet even they were treated like this. As for me, since I don't even qualify as an old tenant, it goes without saying that I'm in an even worse position. Why? First, I'm just a new tenant who's only lived here for four months. I've hardly ever talked to the landladies. Even though I usually love children, I don't pay much attention to their grandson. You could say there's absolutely no "affection" between us. Second, I live in a亭子间 like a pigeon coop. As soon as a rental notice is posted, someone will rent it. It's very convenient and definitely not as difficult as renting out the front building's厢房. Therefore, isn't there a very good chance that I'll be "forced to move out"?

"Who is it? Coming." Someone knocked on the door, and Mrs. Wu, the round-faced landlady, entered in response.

"Mr. Zeng, why do you keep the door closed so tightly, not letting any air in?" she said calmly.

"Yes, I have a bit of a headache..."

Needless to say, as soon as I saw the landlady standing in front of me, I couldn't help but shiver, naturally feeling very embarrassed, so I just replied casually. In fact, using a headache as an excuse wasn't a very clever thing to say. If I really had a headache, wouldn't opening the door and letting the wind in be more comfortable? Then she said:

"A headache? A minor ailment, it's nothing to worry about."

"But I was planning to close the door and sleep for a while."

I didn't expect I could be so clever, thinking of this in the moment.

"That's right, you should sleep for a while. You'll feel better soon."

"Thank you, Mrs. Wu! Would you like to sit down for a moment?"

"Alright, you're too kind." She said with a smile that wasn't quite a smile, "But I need to trouble you with something. I wanted to discuss something with Mr. Zeng."

"Okay... okay... okay..." I finally spoke up. Wasn't this about the rent?

"I heard you're very familiar with Mr. Wang from the × newspaper, so I wanted to ask you for a favor."

"What is it?"

"You see, after the Wang family moved out, the big厢房 has been empty for a full two months. If this goes on for much longer, what will we do? I wanted to ask you to place a small rental advertisement for me, which might be cheaper. Saying this, she immediately took out a draft from her pocket. It read:

Superior Western-style house for rent, located at No. ××, Lane ××, ×× Road, one large厢房, with all sanitary facilities. Interested parties please come to this residence to discuss in person. Wu Residence."

"Alright, I'll definitely take care of it."

"Could you get a discount?"

"Mrs. Wu, anyway, this advertisement doesn't have many words. Even if you don't get a discount, what does it matter to Mrs. Wu? Hahaha." So, I thought, hey! If she just smoked one less pipe of opium, wouldn't that save her the money?

"It would be best if it were half price. Please pay for the advertisement in advance and deduct it from the rent at the end of the month."

"Oh! But... alright, alright."

Finally, the landlady left, and I closed the door again. I repeated, "Pay for the advertisement in advance... alright... alright..." But, where is my money? Alas!

Conjecture on the Soul, by Qingfen 240

Science in the twentieth century is flourishing like bamboo shoots after rain. However, despite the vigorous research and experimentation of many spiritualists, the study of the soul has not yet been thoroughly understood, and the question of its existence has not been definitively answered.

Mr. Xie ××, a mathematics professor at our school, liked to tell jokes to us mischievous students during his spare time. The stories he told were always about ghosts, souls, and demons (not comparable to other myths, as they contain quite a scientific flavor). When timid students heard his descriptions, they would often immediately see a ghost in front of them, screaming and running away, breaking the tense and silent atmosphere.

This time, we asked him to speak again, and he agreed to explain the soul to us. I felt that this was worth recording, so I wrote down what he said below:

The human body contains countless cells, and each cell contains several extremely tiny nuclei. After a person dies, the body is like a well-used tabletop with many small holes. The nuclei in the cells fly out of the holes, like dust scattered in the universe. We call them spiritual particles.

The nature of spiritual particles is the same as that of electrons, photons, and telivesian. When a baby is born, its body has many nests scattered throughout. Spiritual particles scattered in space seem to be attracted and drill into them. Gradually, it can make sounds and cry. In this way, countless spiritual particles are scattered throughout the universe.

When inanimate objects in the human world experience unusual circumstances, it triggers a kind of scientific reaction, and spiritual particles drill into them as if returning to their rightful place. When spiritual particles are organized, their actions seem the same as those of humans. The Chinese novels like Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio, which talk about demons and ghosts, although based on fantasy, have a point.

We often hear people say that ghosts who died unjustly appear and cause trouble. (We sat closely together, our eyes fixed on each other.) Yes, because their spiritual particles still have organization in space, they are able to do this. However, over time, they gradually disintegrate from organization into sand-like particles. Their ability to appear and cause trouble gradually diminishes. Conversely, ghosts who died of illness have disorganized spiritual particles, so their ability to cause trouble is small, if it exists at all.

According to Dou Erde's theory of atoms, we can understand that the soul is such a thing.

Our ghost teacher simply exhaled a long-held breath. Our wandering hearts also settled down with it.

On "Appearances," by Bing 241

I read a very small news item in the newspaper this morning:

Lately, groups of beggars have been found loitering day and night near the Chen Ying Shi Martyr Memorial Tower in the Old West Gate, which is quite detrimental to appearances. In view of this, the authorities issued a strict order yesterday to ban them, and the police have immediately evicted them.

Originally, this fact is not surprising, and this news item is even less so. In present-day China, especially in several major cities, the number of beggars is increasing in line with the times. Since there are so many, they inevitably cause incidents. After all, these unproductive, lowly compatriots with dirty faces, tattered clothes, and empty stomachs are an eyesore no matter which side of the street you pass them on. So, they have become regular material for some news reporters, and they have their place in the newspapers every day, alongside reports of tax increases, rent increases by 20%, economic decline, and salary cuts by 20%, as if they were famous people on the move. This is not a good phenomenon, but the authorities only see it as "detrimental to appearances," so the solution is simply to "strictly evict" them. The facts are already very clear, without any need for "analysis."

What I can't help but say is about the "appearances" in "detrimental to appearances." Those who pay attention to world affairs, both great and small, can find this phrase used everywhere, from national laws and heavy penalties to announcements and warnings in small alleys, where it shows off its "grandeur."

It is commonly thought that the phrase "appearances," if expressed in colloquial terms, means "to look at." Its essence is "impressiveness." In terms of origin and usage, it has two versions: positive and negative, coexisting and interchangeable. For example, outside of certain "sufficient" facilities, if one still feels that "there are areas that are not perfect," without actually examining the essence, one must then add something "to enhance appearances." In short, it is "to beautify," meaning the scenery is magnificent, the events are wondrous, and there is something to see. This is purely from an external, concrete point of view. When used in writing, it becomes a spiritual usage, and its meaning gradually becomes mysterious. This is the positive, forward-looking meaning. The negative, however, simply changes the word at the beginning, turning "to beautify" into "detrimental." Just like strictly banning beggars, it is also related to "appearances," but it starts from a negative reduction. In fact, it is also "to beautify appearances," because reducing some incompatible elements enhances the original things. It is only a difference in designation; the essence is two sides of the same coin. Whether it is "to beautify" or "detrimental," the purpose is only "appearances," to show off "appearances."

Let me give you some real examples: when foreign royalty and dignitaries come to China to visit the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum, the authorities must prepare in advance for the sake of "appearances," washing all the places once. If that is not enough, they will add decorations of lights to try to fit the "beautifying appearances." At the same time, in some places where there are few tourists, the grass grows to cover the ankles. Upon inspection, it is truly "detrimental to appearances," so they must quickly hire workers to cut it down overnight, which ultimately boils down to "beautifying appearances," only slightly negative. Also, when assembling troops for a military review, everyone must groom themselves, or they are given new weapons. This is "beautifying appearances." If there are those with bad habits, wearing crooked hats and slippers, this is "detrimental to appearances." Before the review, they must be strictly inspected and either ordered to change immediately or be eliminated and not allowed to participate. This is also a true situation. As for the design of school nameplates, the many humorous announcements at the ends of alleys, and the shop signs, etc., I will not mention them all.

Because the essence of "appearances" is "impressiveness," one only needs to strive for external appearances to finish the job. Whether there are defects in the essence is a minor matter that does not require far-sighted planning or deep investigation. All things in China can be viewed in this way.

In conclusion, I borrow a saying from Confucius's Governance chapter: "Observe what a man does."

A Night of Debauchery, by Huo 242

Having accepted the invitation from several enthusiastic friends, I entered the ×× Grand Hotel for the first time. Under the shining neon lights, I was swallowed by the huge building. Stepping onto the elevator, I muttered "608." Which floor is "608" on? "Sixth floor!" The driver with the iron-blue face stiffly spat out those two words, and I instantly arrived on the sixth floor. Bursting through the door, oh, in the stifling haze of smoke, besides the sounds of laughter, I only heard the constant clatter of mahjong tiles like popping beans. White board, fortune, three doubles, full count. To put it un-exaggeratedly, I am truly a fool. Drifting in foreign lands and sinking in major cities for nearly ten years, I am still a complete outsider to life events such as mahjong, and I even get a headache when I see others playing so enthusiastically, and even get annoyed with them.

"Ah Mu Lin is here!" C gentleman first raised his head, glanced at me, and said:

"So this is how you all are! What kind of appointment is this?" Although I am a bit of a fool myself, I am not used to others laughing at me casually. I was very unhappy and stopped them.

"We were just waiting for you to come. If you hadn't come earlier, we would have started playing first! Why be so serious about life!" That is to say, they were "acting according to circumstances" casually, and they were waiting for me.

After the meal, we returned to the room. Some fell asleep drunk, some loosened their belts after being full, spread their legs apart, and sat on the sofa, like a statue with a bulging belly. Everyone was silent, looking at each other. After about half an hour, everyone opened the conversation box: some reported on their current living conditions, some described their feelings about world affairs, and some chatted about trivial women's affairs. Only W gentleman, who had just come from his hometown, reported on the truth of the collapse of the rural areas, which was most worth listening to: He said that the harvest was abundant, and the grain was only one yuan and three corners per担, but the tenant farmers and owner-farmers were suffering, and their lives were simply unbearable. Salt, which had to be imported from outside, had to go through heavy tax cards and was sold in rural areas for 1,500 cash per catty. The farmers worked hard to grow a担 of rice, but they couldn't exchange it for a few catties of salt, so they had to eat plain food. Previously, the land tax donation was only three yuan for every two饷, but now, due to the additional security team fee, the militia team fee, and the patriotic donation, it has suddenly increased to more than twenty yuan per two饷. The common people cannot pay it, so they can only follow the officers and soldiers to taste the flavor of iron windows, or borrow at a high interest of 5% to delay the payment for one or two months.

As we talked, it was soon late at night, and everyone was tired. A silent atmosphere enveloped everyone's body and mind again.

"Everyone has nothing to say. I suggest we play another four rounds!" D gentleman, who loved this the most, fearing the continuation of silence, stretched and said this. The four of us who didn't know how to play all opposed it, and finally temporarily broke up one of their feet. But as soon as we fell asleep, we only heard the sound of mahjong in the room.

War and Peace (Three) (Six) (Four-Act Play), by Ling He 243

Act Three: Praise of Peace

Military Authority: Easy, easy. Thank you for your praise, I am very honored! … Secretary He, please tell them inside that Principal Zhang has come from Tianjin today, and we should give him a wash-dusting.

Principal: You are too kind, you are too kind, I will go back to Tianjin immediately, and come to visit another day.

Military Authority: Oh? Is the school very busy?

Principal: Yes. I should rush back to explain to the students and the people of Tianjin the true meaning of this truce, that it is by no means surrendering to the enemy, but to preserve our national vitality. Guiding the people in this way is the duty of those of us who run education.

Military Authority: In that case, I won't keep you any longer, because private matters are small and national matters are big. In this national crisis, we should distinguish between light and

heavy. Principal Zhang, is that right?

Principal: That is so, that is so. Okay, goodbye.

Military Authority: Goodbye. I won't see you off. (Secretary sees him off) (Seeing the maid enter from outside) Hey! Go tell Madam to prepare several opium bubbles for me. I'll be there in a while. (Yawns. Secretary enters from outside.) What, you still argue with this kind of person. All you have to do is give him an official position, and he'll be happy.

Private Secretary: Hahahaha. Minister, you are truly a great politician. I couldn't think of that method for a moment. Damn it, what is that thing? He opens his mouth to recover lost land and closes his mouth to continue resisting, which sounds extremely good. In fact, who can't say this kind of thing? Those in the opposition don't know the suffering of those in power. If I were not politically responsible, I would say it even better than him. He's not even ashamed. As soon as he hears that there is an official position to be had, he immediately stops talking big. China has too many of these scholars and celebrities. Just as he was walking to the door, he asked me to mention him to the Minister.

Military Authority: Isn't that just how it is? You think about why he came here, it's still to beg for an official position. All you have to do is give him an official position, give him a few hundred yuan a month, and he will never say nice things again.

Orderly: (From outside) Commissioner Tian is here.

Military Authority: Damn it, I was just thinking of going upstairs to smoke some opium, but he had to come again. (Yawns) Okay, please let him in.

Private Secretary: Then how should today's news be released? The newspaper reporters, who are like jumping fleas, are going to be troublesome again.

Military Authority: Then you think of a way to deal with them. Anyway, it's always these few words. The main thing is to state that this truce negotiation does not involve political or diplomatic aspects at all, but is entirely military. If they want to inquire about the contents of the conditions, then you can very well answer them that there are no formal negotiations at present, so the contents of the conditions cannot be announced.

Private Secretary: These conditions, when we formally negotiate in the future, I don't think they will change much. But how will they be published in the newspaper in the future? We need to consider that now.

Military Authority: Then you go and draft a draft. (Secretary goes down)

Film Special

A Record of Interviews with Chinese Film Artists (5) (Continued from yesterday) 244

— Sha Ji

(II) Zheng Zhengqiu, Director of "The Flower of Freedom" (Part Two)

The above can be said to be his thoughts on Chinese film directors. Afterward, regarding his own works, I sought his opinion in this way:

"Mr. Zheng, what are your thoughts on your recent work, 'Spring Water Love Wave'?"

"Regarding 'Spring Water Love Wave'?" He said with a smile, heavily inhaling from his Capstan cigarette. "Because I was sick at the time, sometimes when my illness flared up during work, I just wanted to finish quickly. Also, because the film exceeded the intended length, I temporarily cut several scenes. As a result, some characters appeared, and the audience felt it was abrupt..."

"Regarding the slogan to go to the Northwest," I asked, "Does Mr. Zheng think it's necessary? In this situation where China's economy is entirely controlled by world powers."

"There is quite a bit of factual basis to it. Before the 'September 18th Incident', there was indeed a Zhang Tianchou who went to Suiyuan to develop the land, and he did well. But after the 'September 18th Incident', it didn't work out.

"Naturally, there are many accidental facts in the world. However, at a time when the Northeast has been completely lost, the slogan of going to the Northwest is ultimately a cowardly hope for artists who have run out of options. Moreover, without fundamentally eradicating the power of foreign powers in China, there is no possibility of realizing this hope. Therefore, the anti-imperialist movement is the biggest task for film today. Instead of putting forward empty slogans, it is better to thoroughly oppose imperialism: especially when the Second World War is about to break out and China will become a slaughterhouse to be divided up."

We talked a lot this time, and I can't record it all. Of his past works, he said he was most satisfied with "The Flower of Freedom," because it was an anti-imperialist work. He is currently filming "The Nobleman and the Criminal," which is adapted from his early new drama (he said: now called civilization drama). He believes this work will not fail. It is a very emotional ethical film, and Hu Die performed very well on stage. However, he is also worried that the actors' lives are not rich enough, and that actors who lack rural life experience will not be able to realistically portray rural people. Here he raised the issue of actor training, and he hopes that various companies can jointly establish an actor training school. However, I personally believe that actors' skills are not learned in the classroom but in practical life, and he agreed with this, which can be proved by the skills of Russian actors. At the same time, he asked this publication to introduce more theoretical materials on acting techniques. Although one or two people in China have written books on this type of teaching material, the actual application of those things is terribly ugly. Most importantly, he opposes double censorship. He is worried that Chinese films will soon be controlled by political deterioration, and then he may not be able to say what he wants to say.

Finally, he talked about his resume: In the early years of the Republic of China, many people returned from Japan and pioneered new drama. At that time, he was the chief writer for the China Daily and often wrote reviews of plays. Later, a Westerner established the Asia Film Company and wanted to hire these new drama people to shoot films, but the conditions were not met. Therefore, through Zhang Shichuan's introduction, he gathered many people, personally wrote the script, and directed the first film, "Difficult Husband and Wife." Unfortunately, the Second Revolution occurred in the second year of the Republic of China, and war broke out in Shanghai, and the Westerner fled in shock. Helplessly, he changed the actors' profession to new drama. Plays such as "The Un-Lover" and "Bitter Milk Mother" were published. This continued for more than ten years. Then, the Shanghai "Xin Jiao" stock market craze prevailed, and the Datong Exchange was organized. After failing, he used the remaining shares to start the Star Film Company, with capital of less than 20,000 yuan at the time. His colleagues included Zheng Zhegu and Ren Jinpin. This was more than ten years ago. ((II) End)

Errata: In the article "The Skills of Actors and Directors and Screenwriters..." published here on the 26th of this month, the section where the word "ut" is missing in the second paragraph. That paragraph should read: "...a sound of "ut" is heard, the result will definitely be very bad. Conversely, when an actor can no longer continue an expression, an "ut" is appropriately made, and of course the result will definitely be unexpectedly satisfactory." This is hereby corrected.

Film Reviews

Review of "Astray" 245

— Ling He

Since Chinese films embarked on a new path in the latter half of 1929, in fact, the entire film industry's artists have been strongly stimulated and followed along this path. Naturally, this is a very good phenomenon. However, if this lineup is strictly examined, it is not only that the pace is uneven, but also that many artists seem to be forced to follow the change helplessly. At the same time, some artists are using "popularization" as a guise in an attempt to succeed in their own preaching.

Regarding this point, we can find proof in "Astray."

What does "Astray" tell us? A worker is fired for attending a "January 28th Incident" memorial service, and his family has nothing to eat, so he becomes a thief, goes to jail, and his wife is bought by a small boss. Here we cannot deny the author's sympathy for the working class. But how does the author explain this problem? In the end, the solemnity of the law is respected, which of course teaches us that the author does not have a deep understanding of the current society, but the author forcibly wants a worker's child to donate his mother's money from selling herself to national salvation through aviation, which is not only a hundred and eight thousand miles away from reality, but also far-fetched and unreasonable.

As for the small errors in the story, they are also common. For example, the factory owner knows that the worker is there to borrow money, but he actually tells him to go into the inner room, but he is not willing to lend him money, why would he bother like this, wouldn't it be simpler to tell him to get lost? Moreover, it is not realistic for a worker to be able to walk into the factory owner's inner room, or even to negotiate with the factory owner in person to ask for leave.

The director's technique is still okay, but he lacks sufficient effort in Montage. Dissolves are used where they should not be used, and the tempo is uneven.

Most importantly, the author's handling of the problem is very conceptual, such as using lewd dancing and drinking to express the decadence of the bourgeoisie. I feel that if a certain problem is grasped at the center, it will never be treated with empty exaggeration in a formulaic way. This aspect shows the author's emptiness of life, and it is ultimately a bold thing to deal with problems that he does not understand himself without actual life experience. Conversely, if the author is only making this kind of popular film for the sake of fashion, then of course it is unthinkable. However, we still have great hopes for the author, Zhang Tianbei.

Review of "London Fragrant Dream Shadows" 246

— He Lian

This film is nothing more than a contrived story that forms a corner of the life of a group of hopeless pleasure-seekers in modern capitalist society and the phenomenon of social depression into a contrived story where all lovers become a good match. Taking the combination of the young Tang Mao, who is sinking in the casino, and the girl Mary, who is in the game venue, as the backbone, and adding Hans, the casino owner, to fight for the inheritance, it expresses the decadent side of urban life in the old style of "no coincidence, no story" that is difficult to avoid in general European and American films. The standpoint of its expression is undoubtedly like many European and American films, which stands on anesthesia, enjoyment, and self-explanation. Therefore, the poor and dark side of urban life is inconvenient to express, so at the beginning, a little bit of the situation of the poor is photographed in a very perfunctory manner, and at the same time, the author also tries to make the audience forget about it in the subsequent enjoyment and coincidental scenes. In fact, this kind of expressive attempt is really unnecessary, and these are like adding feet to a snake - judging from the original expressive standpoint of this film.

Since this film is like this in terms of material selection, structure, and expressive standpoint, the old style is so that there is nothing to recommend in terms of directing, acting, and other techniques. It's true that even if there are good directors and good actors, it is difficult to have excellent new expressions in this kind of film. Of course, in a prosperous city like Shanghai, there must be many people who find it very to their taste. Because they will feel quite interested in this kind of story, this kind of structure, and this kind of expression method.

Review of "The Lost Jewel" 247

— Bai

"After Dark"

--Carlton Cinema--

First of all, I have to explain that the play "The Lost Jewel" is an additional performance by the Carlton Cinema in addition to the premiere of "Midnight Dance."

The facts are indeed the most eloquent. In this day and age, no matter how capable you are, you have to succumb to the economic conditions of this social depression. Recently, major theaters in Shanghai have been competing to promote themselves with song and dance. Undoubtedly, this is powerful proof - that is to say, in order to maintain their business, film merchants have to use women's legs to attract audiences in this crisis in an attempt to prosper their business.

Now let's talk about this film.

This play can be said to use the saying "knowing the face but not the heart" as a principle to expose the sins of modern society. It describes a traveler returning from South Africa who is coveted for carrying jewels, and even stolen. Generally speaking, naturally it

s formation is relatively realistic. However, due to the screenwriter's and director's deliberate display of humor, it turned the play into a hodgepodge, which is really a pity. Just in terms of the following points, it is enough to make us feel unreasonable.

(1) After Henry and Harvey knocked Moulton down, they neither killed him nor tried to move him, but put him on the sofa and waited for Elva to rescue him after a long time. Obviously, this is too far from reality.

(2) Harvey met Henry in the old man's house. At that time, the whereabouts of the diamond were not yet known, and it was also very far-fetched to commit the crime rashly.

(3) Elva saw Harvey knock down Henry in the window, and it was right to go into the old man's house. But after a period of panic, he walked out safely. In fact, I'm afraid it wouldn't be like this, right?

(4) The old man is in this serious situation, but he is still as if nothing happened, and later when the lights are restored and the jewels have not been obtained, Moulton and Elva smile and kiss each other, as if these actions were produced in order to make people laugh.

Therefore, I am not saying too much, this play is so deformed entirely due to the unclear understanding of the director and screenwriter themselves. Although the actors' performances are still faithful, under the control of this kind of plot, it will never satisfy the audience.

However, I have to say it again! This play was originally a side play -- to put it bluntly, this is the so-called added attraction. Anyway, the women's song and dance may be able to repay the audience's price!

Film Novel

Mirror Flower Water Moon Three-Cornered Moon (5) 248

— Bolun

Times are changing so fast, New York is not the New York of the past. At that time: warm hotels were everywhere, and taverns and theaters were lined up. When you went out, you wore a leather coat, with the collar high, and you didn't feel the chill of the cold wind at all. You bought a seat in the first four rows when you entered the theater. Coming out of the theater, either you called for a car, and Ronald held you tightly in the car, you could even hear the beating of his heart; or you could walk home, looking at the windows of the major stores along the way, displaying red jewels, green emeralds, backless evening dresses, black velvet pajamas, dazzling your eyes and not feeling tired in your feet. But now it's different. The road a stone's throw away from the subway station is afraid to walk because of sore feet. All the hotels in the city are gone, only relief centers are seen, hungry men standing in a line, one by one going up to receive a piece of bread. In front of the employment agency on Fifth Avenue, it is also full of people. Perhaps you are also standing there, standing for several hours, but to no avail. Sometimes you see a hotel or shop hanging a sign to recruit waitresses and salespeople, but you can't hide it from the boss in the shop. If you haven't fried beef patties, you won't fry beef patties; if you haven't sold socks, you don't know how to sell them either.

Elizabeth was lucky, she met a Granny. With Granny's planning, Elizabeth was able to impersonate an experienced female worker and found a job in a shoe factory. On the first day of work, the foreman looked at her intently. From the foreman's hungry tiger-like gaze, she realized that he was looking at her, from her feet, past her thighs, to her waist, the curves of her youthful body had been seen through by him at a glance. Her face immediately turned red, and she was so shy that she wanted to hide: but thinking that on Friday when she got her salary, she could buy bread and beef to feed the Linberga family, she finally felt at ease to work. Moreover, there is also Ronald's future, how can she not consider it?

Soon Douglas found a small job in the theater. His job only required him to say the word Yes. So he practiced all kinds of ways to say Yes all day long. If he didn't believe or looked down on people, he would also say yes in the same way, but with a different kind of performance expression. The younger brother, Aidi, also found a job as an assistant in a children's playground. He was busy all day long, and his wages were one dollar a day. Douglas was not much better, his wages were twelve dollars a week.

At this time, the Lindberga's parlor was no longer a place for people to gather. The most comfortable sofa, the phonograph, the large dressing mirror, and Elizabeth's favorite green blanket have all been sold. The grandmother's grandfather clock has been returned to a wealthy family on Pike Street as a decoration. The good thing is that they can already not worry about hunger. They eat beef patties every Tuesday, fried saury every Wednesday, and braised beef every Thursday. But when she thought of steak, Elizabeth looked outside the door of the butcher shop. She comforted herself that steak had not disappeared and that there would be a day when she could eat it. But whether their fate is getting better day by day is still a question; even Elizabeth's work in the shoe factory is not a long-term situation, and she still has to guard against the foreman's constant frivolousness and seduction. (To be continued)
